until\\n241:      * authentication succeeds or fails.\\n242:      *\\n243:      * The messages are sent and received as size delimited bytes that consists of a 4 byte network-ordered size N\\n244:      * followed by N bytes representing the opaque payload.\\n245:      */\\n246:     @SuppressWarnings(\\\"fallthrough\\\")\\n247:     @Override\\n248:     public void authenticate() throws IOException {\\n249:         if (saslState != SaslState.REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE) {\\n250:             if (netOutBuffer != null && !flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps())\\n251:                 return;\\n252: \\n253:             if (saslServer != null && saslServer.isComplete()) {\\n254:                 setSaslState(SaslState.COMPLETE);\\n255:                 return;\\n256:             }\\n257: \\n258: connectionId);\\n260: \\n261:             try {\\n262:                 netInBuffer.readFrom(transportLayer);\\n263:             } catch (InvalidReceiveException e) {\\n264:                 throw new      break;\\n285:                     // For default GSSAPI, fall through to authenticate using the client token as the first GSSAPI packet.\\n286:                     // This is required for interoperability with 0.9.0.x clients which do not send handshake request\\n287:                 case AUTHENTICATE:\\n288:                     handleSaslToken(clientToken);\\n289:                     // When the authentication exchange is complete and no more tokens are expected from the client,\\n290:                     // update SASL state. }\\n335: \\n336:     @Override\\n337:     public void close() throws IOException {\\n338:         if (principalBuilder instanceof Closeable)\\n339:             Utils.closeQuietly((Closeable) KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\\n442:             RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\\n443: // This should not normally occur since clients typically check supported versions using ApiVersionsRequest\\n451:                 throw new UnsupportedVersionException(\\\"Version \\\" + version + \\n504:     private boolean handleKafkaRequest(byte[] requestBytes) throws IOException, AuthenticationException {\\n505:         boolean isKafkaRequest = false;\\n506:         String clientMechanism = null;\\n507:         try {\\n508:             ByteBuffer requestBuffer = ByteBuffer.wrap(requestBytes);\\n509:             RequestHeader header = RequestHeader.parse(requestBuffer);\\n510:             ApiKeys apiKey = header.apiKey();\\n511: \\n512:             // A valid Kafka request header was received. This avoids\\n519:             // unnecessary exposure to some of the more complex schema types.\\n520:             if (apiKey != ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS && apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_HANDSHAKE)\\n521:                 throw new IllegalSaslStateException(\\\"Unexpected Kafka request of type \\\" + apiKey + \\\" during SASL handshake.\\\");\\n522: \\n523:             LOG.debug(\\\"Handling Kafka request {} during {}\\\", apiKey, reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText());\\n524: \\n525: \\n526:             RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\\n527:                     KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\\n528:             RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\\n529:             if (apiKey == ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS)\\n530:                 handleApiVersionsRequest(requestContext, (ApiVersionsRequest) requestAndSize.request);\\n531:             else\\n532:                 clientMechanism = handleHandshakeRequest(requestContext, (SaslHandshakeRequest) requestAndSize.request);\\n533:         } catch (InvalidRequestException e) {\\n534:             if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST) {\\n535:                 // InvalidRequestException is thrown if the request is not in Kafka format or if the API key\\n536:                 // is invalid. (LOG.isDebugEnabled()) {\\n539:                     StringBuilder tokenBuilder = new StringBuilder();\\n540:                     for (byte b : requestBytes) {\\n541:                         tokenBuilder.append(String.format(\\\"%02x\\\", b));\\n542:                         if (tokenBuilder.length() >= 20)\\n543:                              break;\\n544:                     }\\n545:                     LOG.debug(\\\"Received client packet of length {} starting with bytes 0x{}, process as GSSAPI packet\\\", requestBytes.length, tokenBuilder);\\n546:                 }\\n547: UnsupportedSaslMechanismException(\\\"Exception handling first SASL packet from client, GSSAPI is not supported by server\\\", e);\\n552:             } else\\n553:                 throw e;\\n554: handleHandshakeRequest(RequestContext context, SaslHandshakeRequest handshakeRequest) throws IOException, UnsupportedSaslMechanismException {\\n564:         String clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism();\\n565:         short version = context.header.apiVersion();\\n566:         if (version >= 1)\\n567:             this.enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders(true);\\n568:         if (enabledMechanisms.contains(clientMechanism)) {\\n569:             LOG.debug(\\\"Using SASL mechanism '{}' provided by client\\\", This looks correct.\n\nLine 152: `verifyClientProof(clientFinalMessage);`\n- This calls the verification method.\n\nLine 225-234: `verifyClientProof` method:\n- Uses `MessageDigest.isEqual(computedStoredKey, expectedStoredKey)` which is good for timing attack protection.\n- But wait, let me look at the logic more carefully.\n\nLooking at line 225-234:\n```java\nprivate void verifyClientProof(ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage) throws SaslException {\n    try {\n        byte[] expectedStoredKey = scramCredential.storedKey();\n        byte[] clientSignature = formatter.clientSignature(expectedStoredKey, clientFirstMessage, serverFirstMessage, clientFinalMessage);\n        byte[] computedStoredKey = formatter.storedKey(clientSignature, clientFinalMessage.proof());\n        if (!MessageDigest.isEqual(computedStoredKey, expectedStoredKey))\n            throw new SaslException(\"Invalid client credentials\");\n    } catch (InvalidKeyException e) {\n        throw new SaslException(\"Sasl client verification failed\", e);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe logic seems to be:\n\n\n1. Get the expected stored key from the credential\n2. Compute the client signature using the expected stored key\n3. Compute the stored key from the client signature and proof\n4. Compare the computed stored key with the expected stored key\n\nWait, this looks suspicious! In SCRAM, the flow should be:\n- Client sends proof which is: ClientProof = ClientKey XOR ClientSignature\n- Server should compute: ClientSignature = HMAC(StoredKey, AuthMessage)\n- Then: ClientKey = ClientProof XOR ClientSignature\n- Then verify: StoredKey = H(ClientKey)\n\nBut the code is computing the stored key from the client signature and proof, which seems backwards. The verification logic appears to have the SCRAM algorithm flow inverted - it's deriving the stored key from the proof instead of deriving the client key and then verifying it matches the stored key. This is calling storedKey with clientSignature and proof, which doesn't align with the SCRAM specification. The storedKey should be derived from the ClientKey, not computed from those two values.\n\nIn SCRAM, the verification flow should be: compute ClientSignature using HMAC(StoredKey, AuthMessage), then derive ClientKey by XORing the proof with that signature, and finally verify that hashing the derived ClientKey matches the stored key. The current implementation appears to be attempting something different with how it's combining these values. So the formatter is computing `H(proof XOR clientSignature)` to derive the stored key. The verification flow makes sense: it uses the expected stored key to compute what the client signature should be, then XORs that with the proof from the message to recover the client key, and finally hashes it to get the computed stored key for comparison.\n\nBut I'm noticing something else—there's token expiry handling at line 121 where the timestamp gets stored, and later at lines 189-190 it returns that value when requested. However, I don't see any actual validation that checks whether the token has actually expired before accepting it. That seems like a potential security gap. The token expiry timestamp gets retrieved and stored, but there's no validation that it hasn't already passed. This is a security gap—an expired token could still be accepted, potentially allowing authentication bypass with delegation tokens.\n\nLooking at the second file, I see `enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders` being set to true at line 567, which just toggles a flag. The code does check whether token authentication was used via `ScramMechanism.isScram()` and marks the principal accordingly, which appears correct. When a request arrives at line 514-515, if it's in INITIAL_REQUEST state, it transitions to HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST. But the code also handles the case where the initial request is actually a GSSAPI token rather than a Kafka handshake—if `handleKafkaRequest()` returns false, execution falls through to the AUTHENTICATE case and processes the token directly. This design accommodates older clients that skip the handshake and send GSSAPI packets immediately.\n\nScanning through the validation logic, I see error handling for invalid API versions requests at line 592-593, which properly sends error responses. The `handleSaslToken` method and the `handleHandshakeRequest` method both appear to be where the actual SASL mechanism negotiation happens, so those are worth examining more closely for potential issues. Looking at the state transitions, when an initial Kafka request arrives, the state moves from INITIAL_REQUEST to HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST.
